Faith and Disbelief
beginner
4 min
The Muqallid's Faith: Worldly vs. Afterlife Rulings
Explains the condition of the muqallid's faith and distinguishes between worldly and afterlife rulings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between worldly and afterlife rulings regarding the faith of a muqallid and why firm conviction is necessary for salvation.

Core Idea
Worldly Islam requires only affirmation; true faith requires certainty.

This lesson addresses two crucial questions. First, does blind imitation (taqlid) suffice for faith? Second, does the same standard apply in this world and the next? The answer is nuanced. While a mere follower without certainty is not a true believer in the sight of Allah, outwardly he is still treated as a Muslim. Understanding this distinction is key to avoiding both extremism and negligence.

Guided Path
1
Understand the condition of the muqallid
Read the passage carefully to see what it says about a muqallid who lacks firm conviction. Note that his belief is insufficient for the validity of his Islam because he remains in doubt, which contradicts iman.
The author emphasizes that scholars are agreed on the invalidity of his faith for the afterlife.
2
Note the agreement among scholars
The passage states that the scholars are unanimous on this point—there is no disagreement that such a muqallid's faith is invalid for the afterlife.
3
Grasp the worldly vs. afterlife distinction
The disagreement among scholars only pertains to the afterlife rulings. For this world, the sufficient level of faith is merely verbal affirmation (al-iqrar).
This distinction means that for worldly interactions, we judge by outward appearance.
4
Apply the rule: outward actions matter
If a person affirms the shahada, Islamic rulings apply to him in this world unless he performs an action indicating disbelief, such as prostrating to an idol.
This shows that worldly rulings are based on external manifestation, not inner certainty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تعيين أول واجب على المكلف وبيان الخلاف فيه
(والا)، أي: وإن لم يجزم المقلّد اعتقاده بما أخبره به الغير على الوجه السابق (۱) ، لم يَكْفِه ذلك الاعتقاد في صحة إسلامه وتَرتُبِ أحكامه عليه لأنَّه (لَمْ يَزَلْ) واقعا (فِي الضَّيْرِ) ، أي : في ضَيْر الشَّكَ المُنافي للإيمان ، لم يتخلص منه ، وهذا ليس مِن محل الخلاف في شيء ؛ لأنَّهم متفقون على عدم صحة إيمانه .
والخلاف في إيمان المقلد إنما هو بالنظر إلى أحكام الآخرة وفيما عند الله ، وأما بالنظر إلى أحكام الدُّنيا ؛ فالإيمانُ الكافي فيها هو الإقرار فقط، فمَن أقرَّ أُجريت عليه الأحكام الإسلاميَّة في الدُّنيا ، ولمْ يُحكم عليه بكُفرٍ ، إلا إذا اقترن به فعل يدلّ على كفره ، كالسجود للصنم .
Determination of the first obligatory duty upon the accountable person and clarification of the disagreement concerning it. (Otherwise), meaning: if the muqallid (blind follower) does not firmly believe in his conviction in what he was informed by another in the aforementioned manner, that belief does not suffice him for the validity of his Islam and the application of its rulings upon him, because he remains in ضير (distress), i.e., in the distress of doubt that contradicts faith, not freed from it. This is not at all part of the disagreement; for they are agreed on the invalidity of his faith. The disagreement regarding the faith of the muqallid is only with respect to the rulings of the afterlife and what is with Allah. As for the rulings of this world, the faith sufficient therein is merely verbal affirmation (al-iqrar). So whoever affirms, the Islamic rulings are applied to him in this world, and he is not judged to be a disbeliever, unless an action indicating his disbelief accompanies it, such as prostrating to an idol.
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage clarifies the concept of taqlid and its effect on faith. It begins by stating that if a muqallid (one who blindly follows) does not have a firm conviction in what he has been told (i.e., his faith is not based on certainty but merely on the report of others without internal assurance), then his belief is insufficient for the validity of his Islam. The author uses the phrase 'لم يزل واقعا في الضير' meaning he remains in the distress of doubt, which contradicts true iman (faith). The scholars are agreed on this: such a person's iman is not valid in the sight of Allah. However, the passage then makes a critical distinction: the disagreement among scholars only pertains to the rulings of the afterlife (al-akhira) and what is with Allah. Regarding the rulings of this world (al-dunya), the sufficient level of iman is merely verbal affirmation (al-iqrar). As long as a person outwardly declares the shahada, he is treated as a Muslim in this world, and Islamic rulings apply to him, unless he performs an act that clearly indicates kufr, such as prostrating to an idol. This distinction is important because it shows that for worldly interactions, we judge by the outward appearance, while ultimate judgment belongs to Allah.

Key Terms
مقلد
إيمان
إقرار
أحكام الدنيا
أحكام الآخرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That any level of imitation suffices for true faith.
Correction: Without certainty, faith is invalid for the afterlife, though it may be sufficient for worldly rulings.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is required for a muqallid's faith to be valid in the afterlife?
A) Mere verbal affirmation (iqrar)
B) A firm conviction without doubt
C) Following a scholar without question
D) Both A and C

Key Takeaway
A muqallid's faith suffices for worldly rulings by mere affirmation, but for the afterlife, firm conviction is required.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you satisfied with merely being called a Muslim by those around you, or have you personally sought the certainty that saves you on the Day of Judgment? What specific steps will you take this week to move from blind imitation to firm conviction?
?
The passage warns that doubt contradicts faith. Is there any aspect of your belief that you have not examined because it’s uncomfortable? How will you confront that doubt today?
?
If Allah were to ask you tonight, 'Why should I admit you into Paradise?' would your answer rely on what others told you or on the certainty that has taken root in your heart? What will you change starting now?

Faith and Disbelief

Faith as Heartfelt Affirmation
Definition of faith as tasdiq and its relation to Islam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that faith (īmān) is defined as affirmation of the heart (taṣdīq) and why the inclusion of verbal utterance is a point of scholarly dispute.

Core Idea
Faith is a matter of the heart, not just the tongue.

This lesson unpacks the foundational definition of faith in Sunni theology. The author begins by stating that faith is interpreted as affirmation (taṣdīq) and notes a significant disagreement about whether verbal utterance is part of it. He then explains why faith is given priority over Islam: because faith is the inner conviction that connects to the heart, while Islam is the outward submission that follows. Understanding this distinction is crucial for grasping later discussions on belief and practice.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the key terms: الإيمان, التصديق, النطق, الإسلام. The opening line gives the core definition.
The passage is from a commentary (sharh) on Jawharat al-Tawhid.
2
Identify the definition and the dispute
The passage states that faith is interpreted as taṣdīq. It then mentions that there is a dispute (al-khulf) about the role of utterance (al-nuṭq). Ask yourself: why would someone say utterance is part of faith? The passage does not answer yet, but it sets the stage.
3
Understand why faith precedes Islam
The author explains that faith is mentioned before Islam because faith relates to the heart (foundational), while Islam relates to the limbs (subsequent). Reflect on why inner conviction must come before outward action.
This ordering is deliberate in kalam works.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان حقيقة الإيمان
وفُسِّر الإيمان بالتصديقِ والنُّطقُ فِيهِ الخُلْفُ بالتَّحْقِيقِ
ولما كان الإيمان والإسلام باعتبارِ مُتعلّق مفهوميهما (۱) ـ وهو ما يجب الإيمان به ـ من مباحث علم الكلام ذكرهما المصنف رحمه الله تعالى .. مُقدِّما الإيمان لأصالته لتعلقه بالقلب (۲) ، وتبعية الإسلام له لتعلقه بالجوارح، فقال : (وَفُسِّرَ الإِيمَانُ) (۳) أي : حَدَّهُ جمهورُ الأشاعرة والماتريدية وغيرهم الصلاة أنَّ
Statement of the reality of faith. Faith (al-īmān) is interpreted as affirmation (al-taṣdīq), and the utterance (al-nuṭq) concerning it is disputed upon verification. Since faith and Islam, with respect to the relationship of their two concepts (1) — which is that which must be believed — are among the topics of the science of kalam, the author (may God have mercy on him) mentioned them, giving priority to faith due to its foundational nature because it relates to the heart (2), and Islam follows it because it relates to the limbs. So he said: 'Faith is interpreted (3), i.e., its definition according to the majority of Ash'aris, Maturidis, and others...'
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage begins the discussion of the reality of faith. It defines iman as tasdiq (affirmation in the heart) and notes that there is a dispute (khilaf) regarding whether the verbal utterance (nutq) is part of it. The commentator explains why faith is mentioned before Islam: faith is the inner conviction that is the foundation, while Islam is the outward submission that follows from it. The author then states that the majority of Ash'aris and Maturidis define iman as tasdiq.

Key Terms
الإيمان
التصديق
النطق
الإسلام
القلب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that faith is merely verbal confession, without inner conviction.
Correction: The text clarifies that faith is primarily affirmation in the heart (taṣdīq), and the status of verbal utterance is disputed, implying it is not essential.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the definition of iman according to the majority of Ash'aris?
A) Verbal confession.
B) Affirmation (tasdiq).
C) Acts of obedience.
D) Knowledge.

Key Takeaway
Faith is not merely verbal; it is heartfelt affirmation, and this is the foundational definition in Sunni theology.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson teaches that faith is affirmation of the heart, not just words. When you declare 'I believe' with your tongue, do you honestly feel it in your heart, or is there a gap? What specific steps can you take today to align your inner conviction with your outward profession?
?
If faith is truly in the heart, then consider: are you more concerned with how your faith appears to others or with its reality before Allah? How can you shift your focus inward starting now?
?
The passage says faith takes precedence because it is inner. What if your actions (Islam) are strong but your heart feels empty? What does this lesson tell you about the priority? What will you do this week to strengthen your tasdiq?

Faith and Disbelief

The Ash'ari/Maturidi Definition of Faith
The author explains the first technical definition of faith (Ash'ari/Maturidi) and the internal debate on its criterion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari/Maturidi definition of faith as affirmation (tasdiq) and the debate about whether it alone suffices for afterlife rulings or requires verbal confession.

Core Idea
Faith in the Ash'ari view is inner affirmation, but scholars differed on its relationship to verbal confession.

This lesson covers the first technical definition of faith presented by the author: the position of the majority of Ash'aris and Maturidis. It explains that faith is essentially affirmation of what the Prophet brought, and then delves into a key controversy: does this inner affirmation alone secure salvation, or is verbal confession also necessary for the afterlife? The discussion includes the well-known Ash'ari stance and a contrasting view attributed to Abu Hanifa.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the first definition
Read the Arabic and translation carefully, noting that faith is defined as tasdiq.
Pay attention to the phrase 'التصديق بما عُلم مجيء النبي به ضرورة'.
2
Identify the two positions on manat al-ahkam
Notice the difference between the Ash'ari view (tasdiq alone suffices for afterlife) and Abu Hanifa's view (iqrar is required for afterlife rulings).
The passage uses 'مناط أحكام الآخرة'.
3
Understand the rationale about the stubborn
Examine the argument about why the stubborn person is blamed and how it relates to the definition of true affirmation.
The passage discusses the distinction between affirmation (tasdiq) and mere knowledge (ma'rifa).
4
Reflect on the nuance from Ibn al-Humam
Consider the qualification that the affirmer must be ready to confess when asked, otherwise he becomes a stubborn disbeliever.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أولها - وهو مذهب جمهور المحققين من الأشاعرة والماتريدية ـ أنَّه : التصديق بما عُلم مجيء النبي به ضرورة تفصيلا فيما عُلم تفصيلا، وإجمالا فيما عُلم إجمالاً ، ومع اتفاقهم على أنَّ حقيقة الإيمان هي ما ذكرنا فحسب اختلفوا في مناط أحكام الآخرة: أهو مجرد هذا التصديق أم هو مع الإقرار باللسان ؟ وقد اشتهر أنَّ الأشعري وأتباعه يقولون: إن هذه هي حقيقة الإيمان، وهذه الحقيقة وحدها هي مناط إجراء أحكام الآخرة، والإقرار إنما يشترط عندهم ليعرف الناس به وجودَ الإيمان عند صاحبه وليُجروا عليه أحكام الدُّنيا ؛ أَنَّ التصديق أمر باطني لا اطلاع لغير الله وصاحبه عليه، وعلى هذا يكون مَن صدَّقَ بقلبه وترك الإقرار بلسانه - مع قدرته على الإقرار وتمكنه منه ـ مؤمنا فيما بينه وبين تعالى ، ويكون مقره الجنَّة ، ولكن كمال الدين بن الهمام ذكر أنَّ أهل هذا القول اتفقوا على أنَّ هذا المُصدِّق يلزمه أن يعتقد أنه متى طُلب منه الإقرار أتى به ، فإن طُولبَ ولمْ يُقرّ فهو كافر معاند .
وذهب أبو حنيفة رضي الله عنه إلى أن مناط الأحكام الأخروية الإقرار باللسان ، وأما الأخرس في حكمه كإشارة ؛ فالمُصدِّقُ بقلبه الذي لم يُقرَّ بلسانه يكون مؤمناً ، ولكن إيمانه هذا لا تترتب عليه الأحكام الأخروية، ولعلَّ وجه ما ذهب هؤلاء إليه : أن الله ذم المعاندين بأكثر مما ذم به الجاهلين المقصرين، ولقائل أن يقول: إن الذَّمَّ لأنهم أبوا أن يقروا بألسنتهم ؛ وذلك علامة التكذيب، أو لأنهم أنكروا بقلوبهم، وذلك هو التكذيب عينه، وحاصل ذلك منع وجود التصديق عند المعاند الذي تعلَّق الذَّمُّ به ؛ لأنَّ التصديق الذي يُعدُّ صاحبه مؤمنا هو ضد الإنكار ، وأمَّا الحاصل عند المُعاند المذموم فهو التصديق بمعنى المعرفة التي هي ضد النكارة والجهالة .
المذهب الثاني: ـ وهو مذهب الكرامية ـ أنَّ الإيمان هو إقرار اللسان بالشهادتين لا غير
The first of them — and it is the school of the majority of the investigators among the Ash'aris and Maturidis — is that it is: affirmation (al-tasdiq) of what is known that the Prophet brought necessarily, in detail regarding what is known in detail, and in summary regarding what is known in summary. And despite their agreement that the reality of faith is only what we have mentioned, they differed on the criterion for the rulings of the afterlife: is it merely this affirmation, or is it combined with verbal confession (al-iqrar)? It is well-known that al-Ash'ari and his followers say that this is the reality of faith, and this reality alone is the criterion for applying the rulings of the afterlife, and confession is only required by them so that people can know by it the existence of faith in its owner and apply to him the rulings of this world; because affirmation is an inner matter that no one knows besides Allah and its owner. On this basis, whoever affirms with his heart and leaves out verbal confession with his tongue — despite his ability to confess and his capacity for it — is a believer between him and the Most High, and his abode will be Paradise. However, Kamal al-Din ibn al-Humam mentioned that the adherents of this view agreed that this affirmer must believe that whenever he is asked to confess, he does so; if he is demanded to confess and does not, then he is a stubborn disbeliever. And Abu Hanifa, may Allah be pleased with him, held that the criterion for the rulings of the afterlife is verbal confession, and as for the mute, his ruling is like a gesture; so the one who affirms with his heart but does not confess with his tongue is a believer, but his faith does not entail the rulings of the afterlife. And perhaps the reason for what these people held is that Allah blamed the stubborn ones more than He blamed the ignorant, negligent ones. One could say that the blame is because they refused to confess with their tongues — and that is a sign of denial — or because they denied with their hearts, and that is denial itself. The upshot of that is the denial of the existence of affirmation in the stubborn one who is the object of blame; because the affirmation that makes its owner a believer is the opposite of denial, but what occurs in the blamed stubborn one is affirmation in the sense of knowledge (al-ma'rifa) which is the opposite of ignorance and unawareness. The second school — and it is the school of the Karamites — is that faith is verbal confession of the two testifications only.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage presents two technical definitions of faith (iman) and the debates surrounding them. The author begins with the first opinion, which is the school of the majority of Ash'aris and Maturidis: faith is affirmation (tasdiq) of what is known necessarily from the Prophet, in detail for detailed matters and in summary for summary matters. He then explains that even among those who agree on this definition, they differ on the criterion for afterlife rulings: is it this affirmation alone, or affirmation combined with verbal confession (iqrar)? The well-known Ash'ari position is that the reality of faith is this affirmation alone, and it suffices for the afterlife; verbal confession is only required for worldly rulings because affirmation is inner and cannot be known except by Allah and the individual. Thus, one who affirms in his heart but refuses to confess verbally — while able to do so — is a believer before Allah and will enter Paradise. However, Kamal al-Din ibn al-Humam notes that this opinion adds that such a person must believe that he will confess if asked; if he refuses when demanded, he becomes a stubborn disbeliever (kafir mu'anid). The author then presents Abu Hanifa's view: the criterion for afterlife rulings is verbal confession. For the mute, gestures suffice. So the heart affirmer without verbal confession is a believer but does not receive afterlife rulings. The reasoning given is that Allah blames the stubborn more than the ignorant; the blame could be for refusing to confess (a sign of denial) or for inner denial. The conclusion is that the stubborn person lacks true affirmation; what he has is mere knowledge (ma'rifa), not the affirmation that constitutes saving faith. Finally, the second opinion (Karamites) defines faith solely as verbal confession of the two testifications (shahadatayn), with no inner component.

Key Terms
الإيمان
التصديق
الإقرار
مناط الأحكام
المعاند

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that for Ash'aris, verbal confession is completely irrelevant and that a person can refuse to confess without consequence.
Correction: In fact, Ash'aris require verbal confession for worldly rulings and for others to recognize faith. Moreover, Ibn al-Humam notes that if the affirmer refuses to confess when demanded, he becomes a stubborn disbeliever.

Checkpoint
According to the Ash'ari view as described, what is the criterion for the afterlife rulings regarding faith?
A) Affirmation (tasdiq) alone
B) Verbal confession (iqrar) alone
C) Both affirmation and confession
D) Good deeds

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari/Maturidi school defines faith as inner affirmation, but scholars debated whether this affirmation alone secures salvation or requires verbal confession.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you aware of moments when your inner affirmation of Allah remains hidden, and you choose not to confess it verbally despite ability? What holds you back? Write one specific step you will take this week to openly profess your faith.
?
The passage distinguishes between mere knowledge (ma'rifa) and saving affirmation (tasdiq). Do you merely know the truth about Islam, or does it penetrate your heart to the point of action? Be honest: where is your belief lacking the transformation of tasdiq?
?
The stubborn denier refuses to confess even while knowing the truth. Are there any truths in your life that you acknowledge inwardly but resist outwardly? What would it take for you to align your tongue with your heart?

Faith and Disbelief

The Karamite Definition of Faith
The author presents the Karamite definition of faith as verbal confession only.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Karamite position that faith is solely verbal confession of the two testifications.

Core Idea
For the Karamites, faith is only what comes out of the mouth, not what is in the heart.

This lesson presents the second technical definition of faith, that of the Karamites, who held that faith is nothing more than verbal confession of the shahadatayn. This view contrasts sharply with the Ash'ari/Maturidi emphasis on inner affirmation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation for the Karamite definition carefully.
Note the phrase 'إقرار اللسان بالشهادتين لا غير'.
2
Contrast with the first definition
Notice how this definition excludes inner belief entirely, unlike the previous school.
Think about the implications for who is considered a believer.
3
Reflect on implications
Consider the consequences of defining faith solely by outward speech.
This view was controversial; what might be its strengths and weaknesses?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أولها - وهو مذهب جمهور المحققين من الأشاعرة والماتريدية ـ أنَّه : التصديق بما عُلم مجيء النبي به ضرورة تفصيلا فيما عُلم تفصيلا، وإجمالا فيما عُلم إجمالاً ، ومع اتفاقهم على أنَّ حقيقة الإيمان هي ما ذكرنا فحسب اختلفوا في مناط أحكام الآخرة: أهو مجرد هذا التصديق أم هو مع الإقرار باللسان ؟ وقد اشتهر أنَّ الأشعري وأتباعه يقولون: إن هذه هي حقيقة الإيمان، وهذه الحقيقة وحدها هي مناط إجراء أحكام الآخرة، والإقرار إنما يشترط عندهم ليعرف الناس به وجودَ الإيمان عند صاحبه وليُجروا عليه أحكام الدُّنيا ؛ أَنَّ التصديق أمر باطني لا اطلاع لغير الله وصاحبه عليه، وعلى هذا يكون مَن صدَّقَ بقلبه وترك الإقرار بلسانه - مع قدرته على الإقرار وتمكنه منه ـ مؤمنا فيما بينه وبين تعالى ، ويكون مقره الجنَّة ، ولكن كمال الدين بن الهمام ذكر أنَّ أهل هذا القول اتفقوا على أنَّ هذا المُصدِّق يلزمه أن يعتقد أنه متى طُلب منه الإقرار أتى به ، فإن طُولبَ ولمْ يُقرّ فهو كافر معاند .
وذهب أبو حنيفة رضي الله عنه إلى أن مناط الأحكام الأخروية الإقرار باللسان ، وأما الأخرس في حكمه كإشارة ؛ فالمُصدِّقُ بقلبه الذي لم يُقرَّ بلسانه يكون مؤمناً ، ولكن إيمانه هذا لا تترتب عليه الأحكام الأخروية، ولعلَّ وجه ما ذهب هؤلاء إليه : أن الله ذم المعاندين بأكثر مما ذم به الجاهلين المقصرين، ولقائل أن يقول: إن الذَّمَّ لأنهم أبوا أن يقروا بألسنتهم ؛ وذلك علامة التكذيب، أو لأنهم أنكروا بقلوبهم، وذلك هو التكذيب عينه، وحاصل ذلك منع وجود التصديق عند المعاند الذي تعلَّق الذَّمُّ به ؛ لأنَّ التصديق الذي يُعدُّ صاحبه مؤمنا هو ضد الإنكار ، وأمَّا الحاصل عند المُعاند المذموم فهو التصديق بمعنى المعرفة التي هي ضد النكارة والجهالة .
المذهب الثاني: ـ وهو مذهب الكرامية ـ أنَّ الإيمان هو إقرار اللسان بالشهادتين لا غير
The first of them — and it is the school of the majority of the investigators among the Ash'aris and Maturidis — is that it is: affirmation (al-tasdiq) of what is known that the Prophet brought necessarily, in detail regarding what is known in detail, and in summary regarding what is known in summary. And despite their agreement that the reality of faith is only what we have mentioned, they differed on the criterion for the rulings of the afterlife: is it merely this affirmation, or is it combined with verbal confession (al-iqrar)? It is well-known that al-Ash'ari and his followers say that this is the reality of faith, and this reality alone is the criterion for applying the rulings of the afterlife, and confession is only required by them so that people can know by it the existence of faith in its owner and apply to him the rulings of this world; because affirmation is an inner matter that no one knows besides Allah and its owner. On this basis, whoever affirms with his heart and leaves out verbal confession with his tongue — despite his ability to confess and his capacity for it — is a believer between him and the Most High, and his abode will be Paradise. However, Kamal al-Din ibn al-Humam mentioned that the adherents of this view agreed that this affirmer must believe that whenever he is asked to confess, he does so; if he is demanded to confess and does not, then he is a stubborn disbeliever. And Abu Hanifa, may Allah be pleased with him, held that the criterion for the rulings of the afterlife is verbal confession, and as for the mute, his ruling is like a gesture; so the one who affirms with his heart but does not confess with his tongue is a believer, but his faith does not entail the rulings of the afterlife. And perhaps the reason for what these people held is that Allah blamed the stubborn ones more than He blamed the ignorant, negligent ones. One could say that the blame is because they refused to confess with their tongues — and that is a sign of denial — or because they denied with their hearts, and that is denial itself. The upshot of that is the denial of the existence of affirmation in the stubborn one who is the object of blame; because the affirmation that makes its owner a believer is the opposite of denial, but what occurs in the blamed stubborn one is affirmation in the sense of knowledge (al-ma'rifa) which is the opposite of ignorance and unawareness. The second school — and it is the school of the Karamites — is that faith is verbal confession of the two testifications only.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage presents two technical definitions of faith (iman) and the debates surrounding them. The author begins with the first opinion, which is the school of the majority of Ash'aris and Maturidis: faith is affirmation (tasdiq) of what is known necessarily from the Prophet, in detail for detailed matters and in summary for summary matters. He then explains that even among those who agree on this definition, they differ on the criterion for afterlife rulings: is it this affirmation alone, or affirmation combined with verbal confession (iqrar)? The well-known Ash'ari position is that the reality of faith is this affirmation alone, and it suffices for the afterlife; verbal confession is only required for worldly rulings because affirmation is inner and cannot be known except by Allah and the individual. Thus, one who affirms in his heart but refuses to confess verbally — while able to do so — is a believer before Allah and will enter Paradise. However, Kamal al-Din ibn al-Humam notes that this opinion adds that such a person must believe that he will confess if asked; if he refuses when demanded, he becomes a stubborn disbeliever (kafir mu'anid). The author then presents Abu Hanifa's view: the criterion for afterlife rulings is verbal confession. For the mute, gestures suffice. So the heart affirmer without verbal confession is a believer but does not receive afterlife rulings. The reasoning given is that Allah blames the stubborn more than the ignorant; the blame could be for refusing to confess (a sign of denial) or for inner denial. The conclusion is that the stubborn person lacks true affirmation; what he has is mere knowledge (ma'rifa), not the affirmation that constitutes saving faith. Finally, the second opinion (Karamites) defines faith solely as verbal confession of the two testifications (shahadatayn), with no inner component.

الإيمان
الإقرار
الشهادتان
الكَرّامية

Key Takeaway
The Karamites defined faith as nothing more than verbal confession of the two testifications.

?

Defending Iman as Tasdiq Against the Variance Objection
Al-Laqqani presents an objection about the variance of iman among people and gives two answers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Laqqani defends the definition of iman as tasdiq alone against the objection that iman varies among people, using two main answers and a third from other scholars.

Core Idea
Variance in iman does not prove works are part of it—tasdiq alone accounts for differences.

This passage presents an objection raised by those who include works in the definition of iman: if iman is mere tasdiq (attestation), why does it clearly vary among people, from the Prophet (peace be upon him) to ordinary believers? Al-Laqqani gives two internal answers and notes a third answer from other scholars like Imam al-Nawawi. By examining these responses, you will see how tasdiq alone can explain observed differences without needing to add works.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
The objectors argue that if iman is only inner tasdiq, it should be equal for all believers, yet the Prophet's faith is obviously greater. Understand this challenge before seeing the answers.
The objection relies on the observed fact that believers differ in the strength of their faith.
2
Examine the first answer: denial of variance
The first answer simply denies that there is any real difference: either a person has certainty (iman) or lacks it (kufr). Any decrease in certainty is disbelief, not lesser faith.
This answer maintains a strict binary view of iman.
3
Examine the second answer: variance in tasdiq's object and circumstances
The second answer concedes variance but locates it within tasdiq itself: not in its essence, but in its object (muta'allaq) or in the presence of heedlessness. Some believers know more details of what must be believed; others are sometimes heedless.
This answer preserves the definition of iman as tasdiq while explaining differences.
4
Note the third answer from other scholars
A group of scholars, including Imam al-Nawawi, added that tasdiq itself can increase and decrease through reflection, evidence, expansion of the chest, and illumination of the heart. This is another way to account for variance within tasdiq alone.
The passage cuts off here, but the point is clear: intensity of tasdiq can vary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد أورد القائلون بأنَّ الطاعات من الإيمان وجوها استدلوا بها ، نرى أن نذكرها لك أيضاً، ونبين ما في الاستدلال بها من خلل ؛ لتكون على بصيرة تامة في هذه المسألة. قالوا: لو كان الإيمان عبارةٌ عن التصديق الذي هو الإذعان والقبول والاعتراف ؛ لما اختلف في بعض المكلفين عنه في بعضهم الآخر، أنا نعتقد أَنَّ إيمان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ليس مثله في بعضهم إيمان أحدٍ من العامة ، بل ولا الخاصة (وانظر ص ٦١ من حاشية الشارح). ويجاب عن هذا بأحد جوابين: الأول: أَنْ نَدعي أنه لا اختلاف بين إيمان أحد وأحد ، وليس لنا إلا إيمان أو كفر ، فإن بلغ ما عند المكلف إلى حد الجزم الذي لا يعتريه شكٍّ ولا تردُّد فهو مؤمن ، وإن نقص عن ذلك فهو كافر . الثاني : أنْ تُسلَّمَ الاختلاف بين إيمان بعض المكلفين وبعضهم الآخر، لكن لا نسلم أن هذا الاختلاف بسبب أن أعمال بعض المكلفين أكثر أو أشدّ إخلاصاً أو نحو ذلك ، بل سبب الاختلاف راجع إلى التصديق لا باعتبار ذاته ، بل باعتبار متعلقه ، فقد يعلم بعض المكلفين تفصيل شيء مما يجب الإيمان به أكثر مما يعلمه آخر، أو سبب الاختلاف هو أنَّ بعض المكلفين تعتريه الغفلة أحيانًا وبعضهم لا تعتريه الغفلة أصلا ، أو غير ذلك . وسنعود لذلك الموضوع مرة أخرى (٦٢). وقد أجابَ جماعةٌ مِن المحققين - منهم الإمام النووي في شرحه على البخاري ـ بأنَّا نُسلم تفاوت المكلفين في الإيمان مع تمسكنا بأنَّ الإيمان هو التصديق وحده ، ونقول: إن التصديق يزيد وينقص بكثرة النظر وتظاهر الأدلة وانشراح الصدر واستنارة القلب؛ حتى لا تعتري=
And those who say that acts of obedience are from faith have advanced proofs with which they argue. We think we should mention them for you as well, and show the flaw in using them as evidence, so that you may have complete insight into this issue. They said: If faith were the attestation which is submission, acceptance, and recognition, then it would not differ among some responsible persons (mukallafin) compared to others. We believe that the faith of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) is not like the faith of any common person, nor even of the elite. And this is answered by one of two answers: First: that we claim there is no difference between the faith of one person and another; we have only faith or disbelief. If what a person possesses reaches the level of certainty that is not affected by doubt or hesitation, then he is a believer. If it falls short of that, then he is a disbeliever. Second: that we concede the difference between the faith of some responsible persons and others, but we do not concede that this difference is because the deeds of some are more numerous or more sincere or the like. Rather, the cause of difference goes back to the attestation (tasdiq), not considered in itself, but considered in relation to its object (muta'allaq). For some responsible persons may know the details of something that must be believed more than another knows. Or the cause of difference is that some responsible persons are overtaken by heedlessness at times while others are not overtaken by heedlessness at all, or other [causes]. And we will return to this topic again (62). And a group of verifying scholars - among them Imam al-Nawawi in his commentary on al-Bukhari - answered that we concede the variation of responsible persons in faith while adhering to the view that faith is attestation alone, and we say: Attestation increases and decreases by much reflection, the multiplicity of evidences, the expansion of the chest, and the illumination of the heart; so that it is not overtaken by...
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage presents an objection raised by those who include works in the definition of iman. They argue: if iman is mere tasdiq (submission, acceptance, recognition), then it would be the same for all believers; yet we observe that the faith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) is far greater than that of common people or even the elite. Therefore, iman must include works to account for this variance. The author gives two answers. The first answer denies variance altogether: iman is either present (certainty without doubt) or absent (kufr); any deficiency in certainty means disbelief, not lesser faith. The second answer accepts variance but locates its cause within tasdiq itself: not in the essence of tasdiq, but in its object (muta'allaq) or in the presence of heedlessness. Some believers know more details of what must be believed; others are sometimes heedless. He then adds that a group of scholars, including Imam al-Nawawi, offer a third response: tasdiq itself increases and decreases through reflection, evidence, expanded chest, and illumination of the heart. The text cuts off before completing this point, but the argument is that tasdiq can be stronger or weaker due to these factors, without needing to include works.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If iman is only inner tasdiq, it cannot vary among people because it is a single mental act.
Correction: Tasdiq can vary in strength and in the extent of its object (muta'allaq), and can be affected by heedlessness, so variance does not require including works.

Key Takeaway
The objection of variance in iman is answered by either denying the variance or by explaining that tasdiq varies in its object or intensity, not by adding works.

Two Quranic Proofs that Actions Are Not Part of Faith
Author presents two Quranic proofs that faith is only tasdiq, not including works.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand two Quranic proofs that actions are not part of the reality of faith, and how the principle of conjunction supports this distinction.

Core Idea
Faith is inner conviction; actions are distinct, as shown by Quranic evidence.

The author presents two clear arguments from the Quran that 'faith' (iman) refers to belief (tasdiq) alone, not including deeds. The first uses the example of fighting believers; the second relies on the grammatical rule of conjunction. These proofs establish the Islamic theological position that works are separate from the essence of faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Get a sense of the two proofs and the transition.
2
Examine the first proof from Surah al-Hujurat
Notice the verse addresses 'believers' who are fighting. Ask: If actions were part of faith, would they still be called believers? The author says the reality of faith would be negated if a part were missing.
This proof shows that even committing a major sin does not remove belief.
3
Examine the second proof from conjunction
The Quran often says 'those who believed and did righteous deeds'. The rule of conjunction (al-‘atf) is that the conjoined item is different from the first; a part is not conjoined to the whole. Since actions are conjoined to faith, they must be distinct.
This is a linguistic argument based on Arabic grammar.
4
Understand the transition to opponents' views
The author mentions that those who consider acts of obedience as part of faith have their own proofs, which will be presented and critiqued. This sets up the next section.
The author aims for complete clarity on the issue.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان حقيقة الإيمان
وَإِن طَائِفَتَانِ مِنَ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ اقْتَتَلُوا ﴾ [الحجرات: ۹] الآية ، ولو كانت الأعمال جزءاً من حقيقة الإيمان لانتفت الحقيقة بانتفاء جزء منها ، ويؤخذ هذا من كلام الشارح أيضا. الوجه الخامس: [كذا في الحاشية بإسقاط الوجه الرابع ، ولعل ترقيمه سهو] أنه سبحانه قد عطف الأعمال على الإيمان في كثير من الآيات، منها قوله تعالى: ﴿ إِنَّ الَّذِينَ ءَامَنُوا وَعَمِلُوا الصَّالِحَاتِ كَانَتْ لَهُمْ جَنَّتُ الْفِرْدَوْس نُزُلًا [الكهف: ۱۰۷] ، ولا شكّ أن الأصل أن يكون المعطوف غير المعطوف عليه فلا يُعطَف أحد المتساويين على الآخر، ولا يُعطَف جزء الشيء على كله ، وقد أشار الشارح إلى هذا الوجه أيضاً. وقد أورد القائلون بأنَّ الطاعات من الإيمان وجوها استدلوا بها ، نرى أن نذكرها لك أيضاً، ونبين ما في الاستدلال بها من خلل ؛ لتكون على بصيرة تامة في هذه المسألة.
Statement of the reality of faith. 'And if two parties among the believers fight' [al-Hujurat 49:9] verse. And if actions were part of the reality of faith, the reality would be negated by the negation of a part of it, and this is also taken from the commentator's speech. The fifth proof: [as in the margin, with the omission of the fourth proof, perhaps its numbering is a slip] that He, exalted, has conjoined actions with faith in many verses, among them His saying: 'Indeed, those who have believed and done righteous deeds – they will have the Gardens of Paradise as a lodging' [al-Kahf 18:107]. There is no doubt that the principle is that the conjoined item is different from the item to which it is conjoined, so one of two equivalent things is not conjoined to the other, nor is a part of a thing conjoined to the whole. The commentator has alluded to this proof as well. And those who say that acts of obedience are part of faith have adduced proofs by which they argue; we see fit to mention them to you as well, and to show what defect there is in their argumentation, so that you may be fully insightful in this matter.
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage is the author's own argumentation on the nature of faith, proving that actions are not part of its reality. It begins by citing a verse from Surah al-Hujurat (49:9) which addresses two parties of believers who fight, demonstrating that they are still called believers despite fighting. The author argues: if works were part of the reality (haqiqa) of faith, then the reality would be negated when that part is missing (since fighting is a sin, but faith remains). This point is also taken from the commentator (al-Sharh). Then the author presents the 'fifth proof' (the fourth is omitted, possibly a numbering error): God often conjoins actions to faith with 'and' in the Quran, as in al-Kahf 18:107: 'Those who have believed and done righteous deeds...' The principle of conjunction (al-'atf) is that the conjoined element is different from the element to which it is conjoined; one does not conjoin two identical things, nor a part to the whole. Therefore, since actions are conjoined to faith, they must be distinct from faith and not part of it. The commentator also alluded to this proof. The passage then transitions, stating that those who argue that acts of obedience are part of faith have their own proofs, which the author will present and critique so that the reader gains full clarity. This serves as an introduction to the subsequent objections and answers.

Key Terms

التصديق
الأعمال
الحقيقة
المعطوف
الطاعات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that 'believers' in the Quran includes all who perform good deeds, implying actions are part of faith.
Correction: The author shows that believers can still be called believers even when fighting (sinning), so faith is distinct from actions. Additionally, the conjunction rule proves actions are separate.

Checkpoint
What is the principle of conjunction (al-‘atf) used by the author to argue that actions are not part of faith?
A) The conjoined item is always inferior to the first item.
B) The conjoined item is different from the item to which it is conjoined, and a part is not conjoined to the whole.
C) The conjoined item must be a synonym of the first item.
D) The conjoined item is always an action, not a belief.

Key Takeaway
Actions are distinct from faith; the Quran conjoins them, showing they are separate realities.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Does your heart hold contempt for them, or do you maintain brotherhood while recognizing their sin? Faith and Disbelief
intermediate
10 min
First Objection: Faith Varies Among Believers
Objection and three refutations regarding variation of faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand three responses to the objection that faith varies among believers, demonstrating that faith as tasdiq (affirmation) alone is compatible with variation.

Core Idea
Faith is affirmation; its variation is in strength, not composition.

This lesson addresses a key objection from those who argue that actions are part of faith because faith clearly differs among people. The author presents three answers, showing that variation can be denied, attributed to the object of affirmation, or explained as internal intensification. This passage refines the definition of faith and protects it from reduction to external deeds.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Understand the initial claim: if faith is mere affirmation (tasdiq), it should not vary; but we see the Prophet's faith is greater, so deeds must cause variation.
Notice that the objection assumes variation implies composition.
2
Study the first answer
The first answer denies variation altogether: either one has certainty (jazzm) and is a believer, or lacks it and is a disbeliever. There is no middle ground.
This answer is strict and binary.
3
Study the second answer
The second answer concedes variation but attributes it to differences in the object of affirmation (knowledge of details) or heedlessness, not to deeds.
This preserves tasdiq as the essence while allowing variation in its scope.
4
Study the third answer
The third answer from al-Nawawi and others explains that tasdiq itself increases and decreases through reflection, evidence, heart expansion, and illumination, supporting the idea that faith is only tasdiq and still varies.
This answer emphasizes internal intensification, not external actions.

قالوا: لو كان الإيمان عبارةٌ عن التصديق الذي هو الإذعان والقبول والاعتراف ؛ لما اختلف آخر، أنا نعتقد أَنَّ إيمان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ليس مثله مع في بعض المكلفين عنه في بعضهم إيمان أحدٍ من العامة ، بل ولا الخاصة (وانظر ص ٦١ ويجاب عن هذا بأحد جوابين: الأول: أَنْ نَدعي أنه لا اختلاف بين إيمان أحد وأحد ، وليس لنا إلا إيمان أو كفر ، فإن بلغ عد ما عند المكلف إلى حد الجزم الذي لا يعتريه شكٍّ ولا تردُّد فهو مؤمن ، وإن نقص عن فهو كافر . الثاني : أنْ تُسلَّمَ الاختلاف بين إيمان بعض المكلفين وبعضهم الآخر، لكن لا نسلم أن هذا الاختلاف بسبب أن أعمال بعض المكلفين أكثر أو أشدّ إخلاصاً أو نحو ذلك ، بل سبب الاختلاف راجع إلى التصديق لا باعتبار ذاته ، بل باعتبار متعلقه ، فقد يعلم بعض المكلفين تفصيل شيء مما يجب الإيمان به أكثر مما يعلمه آخر، أو سبب الاختلاف هو المكلفين تعتريه الغفلة أحيانًا وبعضهم لا تعتريه الغفلة أصلا ، أو غير ذلك لذلك الموضوع مرة أخرى (٦٢). وسنعود وقد أجابَ جماعةٌ مِن المحققين - منهم الإمام النووي في شرحه على البخاري ـ بأنَّا نُسلم تفاوت المكلفين في الإيمان مع تمسكنا بأنَّ الإيمان هو التصديق وحده ، ونقول: إن التصديق يزيد وينقص بكثرة النظر وتظاهر الأدلة وانشراح الصدر واستنارة القلب؛ حتى لا تعتري= المصدِّقَ القوي التصديق شبهةٌ ، ولا يتزلزل إيمانه بعارض ، ويؤيده ما روى البخاري عن ابن أبي مليكة قال : أدركت ثلاثين من أصحاب رسول الله الله كلهم يخاف النفاق على نفسه ، أحد يقول : إنه على إيمان جبريل وميكائيل). ما منهم
They said: If faith were expression of tasdiq (affirmation), which is submission, acceptance, and acknowledgement, then it would not differ… [later] I believe that the faith of the Messenger of God (s) is not like the faith of any of the common people, nor even of the elite (see p. 61). And it is answered with one of two answers: First: we claim that there is no difference between the faith of one person and another, and we have only faith or disbelief. If what the responsible person has reaches the level of certainty that is not affected by doubt or hesitation, then he is a believer; and if it falls short of that, then he is a disbeliever. Second: we concede the difference between the faith of some responsible persons and others, but we do not concede that this difference is because the actions of some are more numerous or more sincere or the like. Rather, the cause of the difference goes back to tasdiq (affirmation), not with respect to its essence, but with respect to its object. For some responsible persons may know in detail a thing that must be believed more than another knows, or the cause of the difference is that some responsible persons are sometimes overtaken by heedlessness and others are not overtaken by heedlessness at all, or other such reasons for that same topic (62). And we will return. And a group of investigators – among them Imam al-Nawawi in his commentary on al-Bukhari – answered: We concede the variation of responsible persons in faith while maintaining that faith is solely tasdiq. We say: Tasdiq increases and decreases with frequency of reflection, multiplicity of evidences, expansion of the breast, and illumination of the heart, so that a strong tasdiq of the one with strong tasdiq is not assailed by doubt, nor is his faith shaken by any accident. And this is supported by what al-Bukhari narrated from Ibn Abi Mulayka who said: I encountered thirty of the Companions of the Messenger of God, each of them fearing hypocrisy for himself; not one of them would say that his faith was like that of Jibril and Mika’il.
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage presents the first objection from those who argue that actions are part of faith, followed by three answers. The objection is: if faith were merely affirmation (tasdiq), it would not vary among believers. Yet we observe that the faith of the Prophet (s) is far greater than that of ordinary people or even the elite. Therefore, faith must include deeds which cause this variation. The author gives two immediate answers: (1) Deny variation entirely – either one has certainty (jazzm) and is a believer, or lacks it and is a disbeliever; there is no gradation. (2) Admit variation but attribute it not to deeds but to the object of affirmation – some know more details of what must be believed, or are more heedful, etc. Then a third answer from Imam al-Nawawi and other investigators: they concede variation in faith while affirming it is only tasdiq. They explain that tasdiq itself can increase and decrease through the intensity of reflection, the force of evidence, openness of heart, and illumination. Thus a strong tasdiq is immune to doubt. They support this with a report from Ibn Abi Mulayka that thirty Companions each feared hypocrisy for themselves and none claimed their faith equaled that of angels Jibril and Mika’il – showing variation within affirmation itself. The answer refutes that deeds cause variation; rather, variation is within the core affirmation.

Key Terms

التصديق
الاختلاف
الجزم
الغفلة
النظر
الأدلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Variation in faith proves that deeds are part of faith.
Correction: The author shows that variation can be denied, or attributed to the object of affirmation or internal states, not deeds.

Checkpoint
According to the third answer (from al-Nawawi), how does tasdiq increase and decrease?
A) By performing more good deeds.
B) By the intensity of reflection, multiplicity of evidences, expansion of breast, and illumination of heart.
C) By avoiding sins.
D) By the number of times one recites the shahada.

Key Takeaway
Faith is solely tasdiq, and its variation is due to the strength of affirmation, not external deeds.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Reflect on the state of your own tasdiq right now. Is it strong, weak, or fluctuating? What specific thoughts or habits cause it to weaken, and what can you start doing today to strengthen it?
?
The Companions feared hypocrisy even after a lifetime of service. Do you truly fear for your own faith, or have you become complacent? What would it take for you to feel that urgency?
?
The third answer says tasdiq increases by reflection and evidence. When was the last time you deliberately sat to reflect on a proof of Allah’s existence or a sign in the universe? Are you actively seeking to strengthen your faith, or are you relying on past belief?

Objection from Fisq and Two Rebuttals
Objection and two rebuttals against including actions in faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author refutes the claim that fisq contradicts faith by using two distinct rebuttals: a logical analogy and an appeal to other Quranic evidence.

Core Idea
Fisq does not contradict faith; sin can coexist with true belief.

The opponents raise a second objection, citing a Quranic verse that pairs faith with love and fisq with hate, arguing that this shows fisq is incompatible with faith. The author provides two sharp rebuttals. In this lesson, we will examine both arguments and see how the author defends the view that faith is only tasdiq, not including actions.

Guided Path
1
Read the Objection and the Two Rebuttals
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how the objection is stated and then the two answers are introduced.
The passage contains a verse citation and an analogy.
2
Understand the First Rebuttal: The Analogy
The first answer denies the logical implication by using an analogy: loving knowledge and hating fisq does not mean they are mutually exclusive. Understand why this analogy works.
Focus on the conditional reasoning: 'if this indicated contradiction, then...'
3
Understand the Second Rebuttal: Concession and Counter-Quote
The second answer concedes the implication but argues that it doesn't prove the opponents' definition, because other verses like al-An'am 6:82 show that faith can coexist with sin.
Note the phrase 'we concede' (سلَّمنا) and the use of another Quranic verse.
4
Address the Counter-Objection about Kufr
The author anticipates a possible objection: if fisq doesn't contradict faith, then perhaps kufr also doesn't. The reply clarifies that kufr's contradiction is established by other evidence.
This shows the author's carefulness to preserve orthodox boundaries.
5
Reflect on the Overall Strategy
Consider why the author offers two answers and how they work together to defend the single nature of faith as tasdiq.
This lesson reinforces the core doctrine that faith is affirmation, not actions.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قالوا: مما يدل على أن الأعمال داخلة في حقيقة الإيمان أنه جعل الفسوق مناقضا للإيمان لا يجامعه ، وذلك قوله سبحانه: ﴿وَلَكِنَّ اللهَ حَبَّبَ إِلَيْكُمُ الْإِيمَنَ وَزَيَّنَهُ فِي قُلُوبِكُمْ وَكَرَّة إلَيْكُمُ الْكُفْرَ وَالْفُسُوقَ وَالْعِصْيَانَ ﴾ [الحجرات: ۷] . ولو كان الإيمان هو التصديق وحده لجامع الفسوق والعصيان . ويجاب عن ذلك بأحد جوابين:
الأول: لا تُسلم أنَّ هذه الآية دالة على أنّ الفسوق مناقض للإيمان لا يجامعه ، أفترى أني لو قلتُ : (إني أحب العلم وأكره الفسوق)، دلَّ هذا على أنَّ الفسوق نقيض العلم، وأنه لا يجامعه ؟ فإن دل هذا الكلام على مناقضة الفسوق للعلم دلت الآية الكريمة على مناقضة الفسوق للإيمان، ودون ذلك خرط القتاد .
والثاني: سلَّمنا أنَّ الآية تدل على مناقضة الفسوق للإيمان ، لكن ذلك لا يدل على أن الإيمان هو ما ذكرتم من التصديق وعمل الطاعات عند كل أحد ، وذلك لأن ما دلت عليه هذه الآية بزعمكم قد عارضه ما يدل على ما ذهبنا من مثل قوله تعالى: ﴿الَّذِينَ ءَامَنُوا وَلَمْ يَلْبِسُوا إِيمَنَهُم بِظُلْمٍ ﴾ [الأنعام: ۸۲] . فإن قلت: فإذا كانت الآية لا تدل على أن الفسوق مناقض للإيمان، فإنها لا تدل أيضا على أنَّ الكفر مناقض للإيمان. فالجواب أن نسلم أن الآية لا تدل على هذا ولا ذاك ، وكون الكفر مناقضا للإيمان ثابت بغير هذا الدليل.
They said: Among the evidence that actions are included in the reality of faith is that He made fisq (immorality) contradictory to faith, not coexisting with it – namely His saying: 'But God has endeared to you faith and has beautified it in your hearts and has made hateful to you disbelief and fisq and disobedience' [al-Hujurat 49:7]. And if faith were only tasdiq, it would accommodate fisq and disobedience. And it is answered with one of two answers:
First: we do not concede that this verse indicates that fisq is contradictory to faith, not coexisting with it. Do you think that if I said, 'I love knowledge and hate fisq,' this would indicate that fisq is the antithesis of knowledge and does not coexist with it? If this statement indicates the contradiction of fisq to knowledge, then the noble verse indicates the contradiction of fisq to faith – and that is extremely difficult (i.e., far-fetched).
Second: we concede that the verse indicates the contradiction of fisq to faith, but that does not prove that faith is what you have mentioned – tasdiq and performance of good deeds for everyone. Because what this verse indicates according to your claim is opposed by what indicates our view, such as His saying: 'Those who believe and do not mix their faith with injustice' [al-An'am 6:82]. If you say: If the verse does not indicate that fisq is contradictory to faith, then it also does not indicate that disbelief (kufr) is contradictory to faith. The answer: we concede that the verse does not indicate either of these; the fact that disbelief is contradictory to faith is established by other evidence.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage is the second objection and its two rebuttals. The opponents argue that the Quran in al-Hujurat 49:7 makes faith beloved and makes disbelief, fisq (immorality), and disobedience hateful. They claim that this shows fisq is contradictory to faith and cannot coexist with it, implying that if faith were just affirmation, it could coexist with sin. Therefore, faith must include actions that prevent sin. The author gives two answers. The first answer denies that the verse logically implies contradiction. It uses an analogy: if someone says 'I love knowledge and hate fisq,' that does not mean fisq is the antithesis of knowledge; similarly, the verse only expresses love for faith and hatred for fisq, not that they are mutually exclusive by essence. The second answer concedes, for argument's sake, that the verse implies contradiction, but then argues that this does not prove that faith consists of both affirmation and actions for everyone. Because other verses, such as al-An'am 6:82 ('Those who believe and do not mix their faith with injustice'), show that faith can coexist with injustice (sin) as long as it is not mixed completely – implying that sins do not negate faith. The author then addresses a counterobjection: if the verse does not indicate contradiction of fisq, then perhaps it also does not indicate contradiction of kufr (disbelief). The reply is that contradiction of kufr is established by other evidence, not this verse. The argument defends the position that faith is only tasdiq, and sin does not nullify it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Quranic command to hate fisq means that anyone who commits fisq is not a believer.
Correction: The verse only shows God's disapproval; it does not logically entail that sin nullifies faith. Other verses (al-An'am 6:82) show that sin can coexist with faith.

Checkpoint
In the second answer to the objection about fisq, which Quranic verse does the author use to show that faith can coexist with sin?
A) al-Hujurat 49:7
B) al-An'am 6:82
C) al-Kahf 18:107
D) al-Hujurat 49:9

Key Takeaway
The Quranic pairing of faith with love and fisq with hate does not prove that sin nullifies faith; faith remains tasdiq alone.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you truly believe that your faith remains intact, or do you feel a sense of total loss? How does this lesson challenge you to hold onto iman even in moments of weakness, and what must you do to prevent sin from becoming a habit that dulls your faith?
?
If iman is only tasdiq, why would you still strive to obey God? What does this lesson reveal about the danger of complacency—that you might think faith alone is enough while ignoring the call to action? How will you respond to the fact that sin, though not destroying iman, is still hateful to God?
?
The analogy of loving knowledge and hating fisq shows that you can love one thing and still be aware of its opposite. Does your love for God truly dominate your heart, or do you allow love for sin to coexist without conflict? What concrete step will you take today to strengthen your love for faith and hatred for disobedience, even if your obedience is imperfect?

Third Objection: Major Sins Negate Faith
Opponents argue major sins negate faith; author begins response.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the opponents' argument that major sins contradict faith and the author's initial rebuttal.

Core Idea
Major sins do not automatically remove faith; pity in punishment is not mercy.

This lesson examines a key objection raised against the Sunni position that major sins do not negate faith. The opponents use Quranic verses to argue that the Prophet is merciful only to believers, and since he is commanded not to pity fornicators, they must be unbelievers. The author begins his response by denying the premise and clarifying the intended meaning of the verse.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Read the passage where the opponents state their claim: committing a major sin negates faith. Then read the translation.
Notice the strong language: 'yunafi al-iman'.
2
Identify the evidence
Find the two sets of Quranic verses used: one showing the Prophet's mercy to believers, the other commanding no pity for fornicators. Understand how they are combined.
3
Understand the logic
Trace the logical chain: mercy is for believers; Prophet is commanded not to have pity (ra'fa) on fornicators; therefore fornicators are not believers.
Note that 'ra'fa' is a form of mercy.
4
Examine the response
Read the author's initial reply: he does not concede the premise and begins to explain the verse's meaning. Notice that the response is incomplete in this passage.
5
Reflect on the dispute
Consider why this objection is important for the doctrine of faith and sin. The author's full answer would continue beyond this excerpt.

قالوا: فعل الكبيرة ينافي الإيمان ؛ لأنه سبحانه أثبت للرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم صفة الرحمة بالمؤمنين فقال: وَكَانَ بِالْمُؤْمِنِينَ رَحِيمًا ﴾ [الأحزاب: ٤٣] وقال: ﴿بِالْمُؤْمِنِينَ رَءُوفٌ رَّحِيمٌ ) [ التوبة : ۱۲۸ ] ، وقد أمره سبحانه ألَّا يَرْأَفَ بالزُّنَاة فقال: وَلَا تَأْخُذَكُر بِهِمَا رَأْفَةٌ فِي دِينِ اللهِ) [النور: ٢] فدل ذلك على أنَّ الزاني ليس بمؤمن، وليس لعدم إيمانه سبب إلا ارتكاب هذه الكبيرة. والجواب عن هذا: أنا لا نسلم أنَّ فعل الكبيرة منافٍ للإيمان، ومعنى الآية: لا تَحْمِلَنَّكم=
They said: Committing a major sin is contrary to faith, because He, exalted, established for the Messenger (s) the attribute of mercy towards the believers, saying: 'And He is to the believers merciful' [al-Ahzab 33:43], and said: 'To the believers kind and merciful' [al-Tawba 9:128]. And He, exalted, commanded him not to show compassion to fornicators, saying: 'And let not pity for them seize you in the religion of God' [al-Nur 24:2]. So that indicates that the fornicator is not a believer, and there is no cause for his lack of faith except committing this major sin. And the answer to this: we do not concede that committing a major sin is contrary to faith. The meaning of the verse: 'Do not let...'
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage is the third objection and the beginning of the author's response. The opponents argue that committing a major sin (kabira) contradicts faith. They present a proof from two sets of verses: one shows that the Prophet (s) is characterized as merciful and kind to the believers; the other (al-Nur 24:2) commands the Prophet not to have pity on fornicators when executing the penalty. Since pity is a trait of mercy reserved for believers, and the Prophet is told not to pity fornicators, this implies fornicators are not believers. Thus the act of fornication negates faith. The author begins his answer by denying the premise: he does not concede that a major sin contradicts faith. He starts to explain the meaning of the verse (likely 'do not let pity seize you' means do not prevent the punishment out of pity, not that the person is a non-believer). However, the answer is incomplete in the available text, breaking off mid-sentence. The author intended to further clarify that the verse does not indicate the fornicator is an unbeliever.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think that because the Quran commands not to pity fornicators, it means fornicators are not believers.
Correction: The author clarifies that the prohibition of pity is about not preventing the punishment out of mercy, not about declaring the person an unbeliever.

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet was commanded not to let pity prevent him from carrying out the punishment on fornicators. Is there a sin in your life where you have allowed sympathy for yourself or others to soften Allah's command? What will you do to uphold the law without compromising your heart?
?
You claim to be a believer, but do you truly distinguish between mercy and leniency? Where have you confused showing mercy with tolerating sin in your own life or in those you love? Examine one specific situation and commit to a change.
?
The opponents argued that major sins negate faith. The author denies that. But if major sins do not negate faith, does that make you feel too secure? Are you using this as an excuse to persist in sin? Confess any such tendency and resolve to repent sincerely.

Two Refutations of Fisq Contradicting Iman
Two answers refuting that fisq contradicts iman via Quran 49:7.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand two distinct responses to the objection that fisq (immorality) cannot coexist with iman based on Quran 49:7.

Core Idea
Contrast in language does not imply logical contradiction.

The objectors claim that Quran 49:7 shows fisq is contradictory to iman, implying actions are part of iman. Our author provides two powerful refutations: first, that the verse only shows a contrast of preference, not logical opposition; second, even if it did show opposition, other verses prove that sin does not negate iman. Let's examine these arguments closely.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and the verse
First, understand the opponents' claim: they cite Quran 49:7 to argue that fisq contradicts iman, so iman must include actions that prevent fisq.
The verse lists kufr, fisq, and disobedience together as hated things.
2
Study the first answer
The first answer denies that the verse implies logical contradiction. The author uses an analogy: 'I love knowledge and hate fisq' does not make fisq the opposite of knowledge. Similarly, the verse only shows love for iman and dislike for fisq.
The phrase 'خرط القتاد' (cutting a thorny tree) indicates the argument is far-fetched.
3
Study the second answer
The second answer concedes the verse implies contradiction but argues that does not prove actions are part of iman. Quran 6:82 shows believers can commit injustice (sin) without losing iman.
This answer uses another verse to counter the objection.
4
Address the counter-objection
A hypothetical objector says: if the verse doesn't show contradiction with fisq, then it also doesn't show contradiction with kufr. The author agrees, but notes that kufr's contradiction is proven by other evidence.
This shows the verse is neutral on the issue.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قالوا: مما يدل على أن الأعمال داخلة في حقيقة الإيمان أنه جعل الفسوق مناقضا للإيمان لا يجامعه ، وذلك قوله سبحانه: ﴿وَلَكِنَّ اللهَ حَبَّبَ إِلَيْكُمُ الْإِيمَنَ وَزَيَّنَهُ فِي قُلُوبِكُمْ وَكَرَّة إلَيْكُمُ الْكُفْرَ وَالْفُسُوقَ وَالْعِصْيَانَ ﴾ [الحجرات: ۷] . ولو كان الإيمان هو التصديق وحده لجامع الفسوق والعصيان . ويجاب عن ذلك بأحد جوابين: الأول: لا تُسلم أنَّ هذه الآية دالة على أنّ الفسوق مناقض للإيمان لا يجامعه ، أفترى أني لو قلتُ : (إني أحب العلم وأكره الفسوق)، دلَّ هذا على أنَّ الفسوق نقيض العلم، وأنه لا يجامعه ؟ فإن دل هذا الكلام على مناقضة الفسوق للعلم دلت الآية الكريمة على مناقضة الفسوق للإيمان، ودون ذلك خرط القتاد . والثاني: سلَّمنا أنَّ الآية تدل على مناقضة الفسوق للإيمان ، لكن ذلك لا يدل على أن الإيمان هو ما ذكرتم من التصديق وعمل الطاعات عند كل أحد ، وذلك لأن ما دلت عليه هذه الآية بزعمكم قد عارضه ما يدل على ما ذهبنا من مثل قوله تعالى: ﴿الَّذِينَ ءَامَنُوا وَلَمْ يَلْبِسُوا إِيمَانَهُم بِظُلْمٍ﴾ [الأنعام: ۸۲] . فإن قلت: فإذا كانت الآية لا تدل على أن الفسوق مناقض للإيمان، فإنها لا تدل أيضا على أنَّ الكفر مناقض للإيمان. فالجواب أن نسلم أن الآية لا تدل على هذا ولا ذاك ، وكون الكفر مناقضا للإيمان ثابت بغير هذا الدليل.
They said: Among what indicates that actions are included in the reality of iman is that He made fisq (immorality) contradictory to iman, not coexisting with it, and that is His saying, Exalted is He: {But Allah has endeared to you the faith and adorned it in your hearts and has made hateful to you disbelief, fisq, and disobedience} [Al-Hujurat 49:7]. And if iman were mere tasdiq (assent), fisq and disobedience would coexist with it. And it is answered with one of two answers: The first: We do not accept that this verse indicates that fisq is contradictory to iman, not coexisting with it. Do you not see that if I say 'I love knowledge and hate fisq', does that indicate that fisq is the opposite of knowledge and does not coexist with it? For if this speech indicates the contradiction of fisq to knowledge, then the noble verse would indicate the contradiction of fisq to iman—and that is far-fetched. The second: We accept that the verse indicates the contradiction of fisq to iman, but that does not indicate that iman is what you mentioned of tasdiq and performing acts of obedience in the view of everyone, because what this verse indicates, in your claim, is opposed by what indicates our view, such as His saying, Exalted is He: {Those who believed and did not mix their iman with injustice} [Al-An'am 6:82]. If you say: So if the verse does not indicate that fisq contradicts iman, then it also does not indicate that kufr contradicts iman. The answer: We accept that the verse does not indicate either, and the fact that kufr contradicts iman is established by other evidence.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage is a kalam refutation of the claim that actions are part of the reality of iman. The objectors cite Quran 49:7, where Allah says He has made iman beloved and kufr, fisq, and disobedience hateful. They argue that if fisq is made hateful, it must be contradictory to iman, implying that iman is not mere assent but includes actions that oppose fisq. The author gives two distinct answers. First answer: The verse does not necessarily imply a conceptual contradiction; it only shows a contrast of preference, not opposition. The author illustrates with a parallel statement 'I love knowledge and hate fisq'—this does not make fisq the opposite of knowledge, but merely a disliked thing. Similarly, the verse shows love for iman and dislike for fisq, not that fisq is the opposite of iman. He calls this argument far-fetched ('خرط القتاد', literally 'the cutting of the [thorny] tree'). Second answer: Even if we accept that the verse shows a contradiction, that does not prove that iman is tasdiq plus actions, because other verses, like 6:82, show that believers can have iman while committing injustice (sin), which suggests that sin does not negate iman. He then addresses a counter-objection: If the verse does not show contradiction with fisq, then it also doesn't show contradiction with kufr? He answers that indeed it does not, but the contradiction of kufr with iman is established by other, stronger evidence. Thus, the verse is neutral on the issue.

Key Terms
الإيمان
الفسوق
التصديق
مناقضة
آية الحجرات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any verse that contrasts iman with fisq proves that fisq logically cannot coexist with iman, implying iman includes actions.
Correction: Contrast in language (e.g., love vs. hate) does not imply logical contradiction; it may only express a difference in preference. Other verses show that believers can commit sins without losing iman.

Checkpoint
In the first answer to the objection from Quran 49:7, what analogy does the author use to show that the verse does not imply a logical contradiction?
A) The analogy of loving knowledge and hating fisq
B) The analogy of mixing iman with injustice
C) The analogy of cutting a thorny tree
D) The analogy of the Prophet's mercy

Key Takeaway
The objection from Quran 49:7 fails because verbal contrast does not entail logical contradiction, and other verses confirm that sin does not negate iman.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you commit a sin, do you ever feel that your iman has completely vanished? How does the second argument (using 6:82) challenge that feeling? What does it demand from you now?
?
The author uses an analogy: 'I love knowledge and hate fisq.' In your own life, do you genuinely love iman and hate sin? If not, what is holding you back from that love? What concrete step will you take today to strengthen that love?
?
The author emphasizes that kufr's contradiction with iman is established by other evidence, not by this verse. Are you clear on what separates kufr from fisq in your own heart? Could you be confusing major sins with disbelief, thus losing hope or falling into false security? What will you do to gain clarity?

Major Sin Does Not Negate Iman: Refuting the Quran 24:2 Objection
Answer to the objection that the Prophet's command not to be merciful to adulterers proves they are not believers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the objection that major sin negates iman based on Quran 24:2 is answered by distinguishing between mercy in punishment and mercy in faith.

Core Idea
Major sin does not negate iman; the command against mercy is about enforcing punishment, not about faith.

This lesson addresses a common objection from those who argue that committing a major sin, like adultery, removes a person from faith. They cite verses where Allah describes the Prophet as merciful to believers, but commands not to show pity to adulterers in the punishment verse. We will see how the answer clarifies that the prohibition is about executing the legal penalty, not about the sinner's belief.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Read the objection carefully: it uses two verses showing the Prophet's mercy to believers, and one verse prohibiting mercy to adulterers, concluding that adulterers are not believers.
Notice how the objection constructs a logical contradiction.
2
Analyze the Quranic evidence
Identify the three Quranic verses cited: Al-Ahzab 33:43, At-Tawbah 9:128 (mercy to believers), and An-Nur 24:2 (no mercy to adulterers). Think about their contexts.
The objection assumes mercy in one context equals mercy in another.
3
Grasp the counter-interpretation
The answer rejects the premise that major sin contradicts iman, and reinterprets Quran 24:2 as prohibiting leniency in executing prescribed punishments, not as a statement about the adulterer's faith.
The key distinction is between mercy in punishment and mercy in belief.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قالوا: فعل الكبيرة ينافي الإيمان ؛ لأنه سبحانه أثبت للرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم صفة الرحمة بالمؤمنين فقال: وَكَانَ بِالْمُؤْمِنِينَ رَحِيمًا ﴾ [الأحزاب: ٤٣] وقال: ﴿بِالْمُؤْمِنِينَ رَءُوفٌ رَّحِيمٌ ) [ التوبة : ۱۲۸ ] ، وقد أمره سبحانه ألَّا يَرْأَفَ بِالزُّنَاةِ فقال: وَلَا تَأْخُذَكُر بِهِمَا رَأْفَةٌ فِي دِينِ اللهِ) [النور: ٢] فدل ذلك على أنَّ الزاني ليس بمؤمن، وليس لعدم إيمانه سبب إلا ارتكاب هذه الكبيرة. والجواب عن هذا: أنا لا نسلم أنَّ فعل الكبيرة منافٍ للإيمان، ومعنى الآية: لا تَحْمِلَنَّكُمُ الشَّفَقَةُ بهم على أن تُسْقِطُوا حدود الله تعالى بعد وجوبها.
They said: The commission of a major sin contradicts iman, because He, Exalted, established for the Messenger, peace be upon him, the attribute of mercy towards the believers, saying: {And He (Allah) is with the believers Merciful} [Al-Ahzab 33:43], and said: {To the believers (he is) kind and merciful} [At-Tawbah 9:128], and He, Exalted, commanded him not to have mercy on adulterers, saying: {And let not pity for them restrain you in the religion of Allah} [An-Nur 24:2]. So that indicates that the adulterer is not a believer, and there is no reason for his lack of iman except committing this major sin. The answer to this: We do not accept that the commission of a major sin contradicts iman, and the meaning of the verse is: Let not compassion for them cause you to abandon the prescribed punishments of Allah after they become obligatory.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and its answer regarding the relationship between major sins and iman. The objectors argue that since Allah describes the Prophet as merciful to believers (Quran 33:43, 9:128), but commands him not to be merciful to adulterers (Quran 24:2), it follows that adulterers are not believers, implying that iman excludes those who commit major sins. The author answers by rejecting the premise that major sin contradicts iman. Instead, he interprets the verse about not showing pity in the context of executing legal punishments (hudud): the prohibition is against allowing compassion to prevent the enforcement of Allah's prescribed penalties after they are due. Thus, the verse does not negate the adulterer's iman, only the permissibility of leniency in punishment.

Key Terms
الكبيرة (major sin)
الرأفة (mercy/pity)
حدود الله (prescribed punishments)
الزنا (adultery)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The command to not show pity to adulterers in Quran 24:2 means that adulterers are not believers; therefore, major sin negates iman.
Correction: The verse is about executing legal punishments, not about the faith status of the sinner. Major sin does not remove iman.

Checkpoint
According to the answer, what does the command 'let not pity restrain you' in Quran 24:2 actually mean?
A) Do not show mercy to adulterers at all
B) Do not be compassionate to them before the punishment
C) Do not let compassion cause you to abandon the prescribed punishment after it is due
D) Do not treat adulterers as believers

Key Takeaway
The command to not show pity to adulterers is about enforcing Allah's prescribed punishments, not a statement that they are outside the fold of faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever caught yourself looking at someone committing a major sin and quietly questioning their faith? How does this lesson challenge that tendency, and what specific shift in attitude does it demand from you toward such a person? Write one concrete way you will apply this in your life this week.
?
The objectors used the Prophet's mercy as a proof that adulterers are not believers. Have you ever misused a verse from the Quran to justify a harsh judgment that actually contradicts its broader message? What does this lesson teach you about the danger of taking verses out of context, and how will you guard against that in your own reading?
?
When you hear the command 'Do not let pity restrain you in the religion of Allah' (24:2), do you feel a tension between mercy and justice? How does this lesson resolve that tension for you personally, and what does it ask of you the next time you encounter a fellow Muslim who has been punished for a sin?
